The First has been brieft as the following> ; this is the first with brief: <# Agents’ Intelligence = HIVE + MIND

Through architecture of the agentic coding platforms and engines [talking about our technology utilizing OpenCode engine SDK, plugins, and harness by the way we engineer the runtime, agents’ self governance and constraint the infrastructure that is local-side-safe by agents knowing the hierarchy and the 5 pillars of works], ; through our “WAYS” of “How a harness should work” , not constraint the creativity, the experiment, offering expert-of-the-field and bite-sized, systematic guidance,  and “silent” self-governance and guardrails, building up a network of share-in-mindset longterm adaptive network of MEMS-BRAIN [this is the analogy of how knowledge pieces are collected in pieces and ready to retrieve as one brain]. We allow the most wanders-of-curioristy individuals to explore their ways out of various fields; while these people WEAVE the knowledge fields across, experimenting on a few particular builds and attempting the law of trials and errors; our agents adapt, grow, and ready to dive deep in or expand breadth without a hassle noticed.  

## WE ARE NOT:

- The corporate-spec-driven-frame-work-maniac for the nerds: unlike GSD, BMAD or any framework that at the top 5 most-used requiring users must be adept and constraint into the particular technology and vibe-coding dev trend requiring certain procedures, segregating very clear between “autonomous” = “following strict rules and protocols” → BUT WE ARE READY TO BE SO, as long as the users set us up to.
- The here-you-go-our-all-in-SOTA-harness-allowing-full-autonomous like Oh-my-agents (or Oh-my-opencode OMO in old naming), this framework will bake all in the hard-architecture-of-harness to allow the users develop hard ideas by just throw in docs and let the LLMs auto → we work them out together with users, we make things difficult to smaller down-stream and bite-sized knowledge by help build the foundation first to layer complexity up on.

## THE HIVEMIND PHILOSOPHIES

<aside>
💡

The true intelligent agents are in plural; they must gain **INTELLIGENCE** <of knowing how to be an expert of the particular field, working from hierarchy, aware of relationship etc>  by **COLLABORATION** not only within the **HIERARCHY** of the **HIVE** but also sharing the interactive workloads and knowledge consumption process with the human beings as they grow with, adapt to, and ready to go-all-hell-deep-in as They <agents> and the human beings share the same **MIND**

</aside>

The practice of us is to follow these  

# THE HIVEMIND PHILOSOPHIES

### 1. HIERARCHICAL SUPERIORITY

- everything from documents, workflows, synthesis must be sorted and output to the very systematic file trees
- The hierarchy also mean safe, if the SOT, the evidence or something should exist first must exist before the child can be handle

### 2. COLLABORATIVE DOMAIN

- knowing the domain at work and loop collaboratively means controlling the delegation
- the agents vs subagents not exceeding domains
- the team must report ack and forth → having the same long term knowledge to keep track that’s why it links to 1

—> from 1 to 2 : everything must use the glob and list to see what are available, sense the context before proceeding, when see patterns → ask, 

- when the context is noisy → clear but always having the path of dot md files, git commit, json network to trace what  happened and recompile

### 3. STRATEGICALLY  MEASURABLE

- Everything must address end-2-end, never conclude complete or success when metrics are not quantitative and qualitative
- more than that the metric must proven standards against something
- in terms of guardrails and gatekeeping → must be incremental
### 4. ITERATIVELY GRANULAR

3 only succeed when we break them down small enough and iteratively loop until perfect

- Do NOT re-specify the wave protocol here — it lives in the skill
- Do NOT overwrite session-context-prompt.md — ALWAYS APPEND

**Output:**
```
<skill_content name="hf-context-absorb">
# Skill: hf-context-absorb

# HF Context Absorb

Multi-wave swarm protocol. Parses dense user input (URLs, files, narrative, events, actors) and appends structured content to `.hivemind/state/session-context-prompt.md`.

## Execution Context

Load these skills before starting:
- `hm-detective` — disk file reading (SKIM/SCAN/DEEP escalation)
- `hm-synthesis` — compression and cross-dependency analysis
- `hm-deep-research` — URL extraction and research patterns

## Wave Protocol (summary — see `references/01-wave-protocol-detail.md` for full specs)

| Wave | Mode | Subagents | Purpose |
|------|------|-----------|---------|
| **0: State Load** | Sequential (self) | 0 | Read existing file, compute delta vs new input |
| **1: Outline Formation** | Parallel | 3 (Parser, Matcher, Scanner) | Categorize input, detect overlaps, scan disk files |
| **2: Deep Processing** | Parallel | 2–3 (URL Extract, Narrative, Cross-Ref) | Extract URLs, synthesize narrative, cross-reference |
| **3: Clarification** | Conditional | 0 (AskUserQuestion) | Resolve ambiguities (max 5 questions, skip if clear) |
| **4: Assemble & Append** | Sequential (self) | 0 | Merge YAML, construct XML block, append, validate |

### Wave Gates

- **Wave 0→1:** Delta report computed. If no existing file: clean slate flag.
- **Wave 1→2:** ≥80% of input elements categorized. If fail: re-dispatch failed parser (max 2 retries).
- **Wave 2→3:** Every URL extracted or flagged failed. If >5 unresolved → Wave 3. Else skip to Wave 4.
- **Wave 3→4:** All ambiguities resolved or escalated to `open_questions`.

## Subagent Prompt Envelope

Every subagent receives:

```
[Session Context]
Phase: hf-absorb Wave N
Existing context size: <lines> lines
Goals: Interpret and persist user's dense context into structured session state
Constraints: Tokens don't matter. Accuracy does. Use ALL available tools aggressively.
Input: <relevant portion for this wave>
Wave findings so far: <summary of previous wave outputs>
```

## YAML Merge Rules (summary — see `references/02-yaml-merge-operations.md`)

On append to session-context-prompt.md frontmatter:
- `dates_active` — APPEND today if absent
- `actors` — MERGE-APPEND (check name exists case-insensitive)
- `domains` — APPEND if new
- `sessions_count` — INCREMENT
- `last_updated` — OVERWRITE with current timestamp
- `complexity` — RECOMPUTE: `max(existing, new)`, cap 10
- `absorb_history` — APPEND new entry
- **Preserve ALL unknown existing fields** — never delete fields from other schemas

If existing YAML lacks absorb fields (first run), initialize them alongside existing fields.

## XML Body Schema (summary — see `references/03-xml-body-schema.md`)

New content appended as:
```xml
<absorb-session date="YYYY-MM-DD" wave_count="N">
  <sources>...</sources>
  <narrative>...</narrative>
  <entities>...</entities>
  <timeline>...</timeline>
  <insights>...</insights>
  <questions_open>...</questions_open>
</absorb-session>
```

## Tool Selection (summary — see `references/04-tool-selection-matrix.md`)

| Task | Primary | Fallback |
|------|---------|----------|
| URL content | `tavily_extract` (batch 20) | `brave_web_search` → `fetcher` |
| Library docs | `context7` pair | `deepwiki_ask_question` |
| GitHub repos | `deepwiki_ask_question` | `repomix_pack_remote_repository` |
| Disk files | `hm-detective` SKIM→SCAN | Direct `Read` for <100 LOC |
| Cross-dep | `hm-synthesis` FOCUSED | Manual grep + cross-compare |

## Error Recovery

| Error | Action |
|-------|--------|
| Target file missing | Initialize with YAML + empty body, then resume Wave 0 |
| YAML parse failure | Extract body, reconstruct YAML from scratch |
| URL extraction failure | Flag `extracted="false"`, add to `open_questions` |
| Subagent timeout | Record partial output, advance with available data |
| Write conflict | Re-read, re-merge, re-write (max 3 retries) |

## Anti-Patterns

| Anti-Pattern | Correction |
|-------------|------------|
| Silent overwrite | ALWAYS append. Verify with line count delta. |
| YAML corruption | Re-parse original, merge to parsed object, re-serialize |
| Phantom URLs | Every URL must have extraction attempt + result |
| Ghost actors | Cross-check narrative refs vs entities list |
| Wave skip | Enforce sequential wave progression |

## References

- `references/01-wave-protocol-detail.md` — Per-wave I/O schemas, subagent dispatch templates, transition guards
- `references/02-yaml-merge-operations.md` — Complete merge operation catalog with schema compatibility matrix and examples
- `references/03-xml-body-schema.md` — XML tag definitions, nesting rules, attribute specifications, validation
- `references/04-tool-selection-matrix.md` — Expanded tool comparison with latency and quality tradeoffs

<path>/Users/apple/hivemind-plugin/.worktrees/harness-experiment/.opencode/skills/hf-context-absorb/references/02-yaml-merge-operations.md</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>
1: # YAML Merge Operations
2: 
3: ## Overview
4: 
5: The YAML frontmatter of `session-context-prompt.md` must be updated during each absorb session. All updates are MERGE operations — never overwrite existing values unless explicitly specified.
6: 
7: ## Schema Compatibility Matrix
8: 
9: The session-context-prompt.md may contain fields from multiple sources. **All fields coexist.** Never delete unknown fields.
10: 
11: | Field | Source | Owner | Absorb behavior |
12: |-------|--------|-------|-----------------|
13: | `version` | absorb | absorb | INCREMENT on structural change |
14: | `created` | absorb | absorb | PRESERVE (set once) |
15: | `last_updated` | absorb | absorb | OVERWRITE with current timestamp |
16: | `dates_active` | absorb | absorb | APPEND today if absent |
17: | `sessions_count` | absorb | absorb | INCREMENT |
18: | `actors` | absorb | absorb | MERGE-APPEND |
19: | `domains` | absorb | absorb | APPEND if new |
20: | `complexity` | absorb | absorb | RECOMPUTE |
21: | `absorb_history` | absorb | absorb | APPEND entry |
22: | `phase` | session-context-manager | SCM | PRESERVE (do not touch) |
23: | `phase_index` | session-context-manager | SCM | PRESERVE |
24: | `checkpoint` | session-context-manager | SCM | PRESERVE |
25: | `session_id` | session-context-manager | SCM | PRESERVE |
26: | `started_at` | session-context-manager | SCM | PRESERVE |
27: | `pipeline` | hf-prompt-enhance | enhance | PRESERVE |
28: | `phases_completed` | hf-prompt-enhance | enhance | PRESERVE |
29: | `prompt_lineage` | hf-prompt-enhance | enhance | PRESERVE |
30: | `complexity_before/after` | hf-prompt-enhance | enhance | PRESERVE |
31: | `confidence` | hf-prompt-enhance | enhance | PRESERVE |
32: | Any other unknown field | any | — | PRESERVE (never delete) |
33: 
34: **Rule:** Absorb ONLY modifies fields it owns. All other fields pass through untouched.
35: 
36: ## Field Catalog
37: 
38: ### Fields Updated Every Absorb
39: 
40: | Field | Type | Operation | Example |
41: |-------|------|-----------|---------|
42: | `last_updated` | ISO8601 string | REPLACE | `"2026-04-09T14:30:00Z"` |
43: | `sessions_count` | integer | INCREMENT | `3` → `4` |
44: | `complexity` | integer (1-10) | RECOMPUTE | `max(existing, assessment)` |
45: 
46: ### Fields Updated Conditionally (APPEND if new)
47: 
48: | Field | Type | Condition | Append Value |
49: |-------|------|-----------|--------------|
50: | `dates_active` | list of dates | Today not in list | `[..., "2026-04-09"]` |
51: | `actors` | list of objects | Actor name not found | `{name: "X", first_seen: "2026-04-09"}` |
52: | `domains` | list of strings | Domain not in list | `[..., "authentication"]` |
53: 
54: ### Fields Updated Every Absorb (History)
55: 
56: | Field | Type | Operation |
57: |-------|------|-----------|
58: | `absorb_history` | list of objects | APPEND `{date, wave_count, sources_added, sections_added}` |
59: 
60: ### Fields Updated on Structural Change
61: 
62: | Field | Type | Condition | Operation |
63: |-------|------|-----------|-----------|
64: | `version` | integer | Existing content modified (not just appended) | INCREMENT |
65: 
66: ## Merge Procedure
67: 
68: ### Step 1: Parse Existing YAML
69: 
70: ```bash
71: # Extract YAML block between first two --- delimiters
72: awk '/^---$/{if(++f==2) exit; next} f==1' .hivemind/state/session-context-prompt.md
73: ```
74: 
75: Parse into key-value pairs. Handle multi-line values (after `|` or `>` indicators).
76: 
77: ### Step 2: Compute Updates
78: 
79: ```
80: existing = parse(yaml_block)
81: 
82: updates = {
83:   last_updated: now_iso8601(),
84:   sessions_count: existing.sessions_count + 1,
85:   complexity: min(10, max(existing.complexity, assess_new_content())),
86:   dates_active: existing.dates_active + [today] IF today NOT IN existing.dates_active,
87:   actors: existing.actors + new_actors,
88:   domains: existing.domains + new_domains,
89:   absorb_history: existing.absorb_history + [{
90:     date: today,
91:     wave_count: 4,
92:     sources_added: count(new_sources),
93:     sections_added: count(new_sections)
94:   }],
95:   version: existing.version + 1 IF structural_change ELSE existing.version
96: }
97: ```
98: 
99: ### Step 3: Serialize Updated YAML
100: 
101: Write YAML block preserving original formatting style. Use `|` for multi-line values. Use `[item1, item2]` inline format for short lists. Use block format for long lists.
102: 
103: ### Step 4: Validate Merge
104: 
105: ```bash
106: # Check YAML still parses (delimiter balance)
107: awk 'BEGIN{c=0} /^---$/{c++} END{if(c%2!=0) print "FAIL"; else print "PASS"}' .hivemind/state/session-context-prompt.md
108: 
109: # Check sessions_count incremented
110: NEW_COUNT=$(awk '/^sessions_count:/{print $2}' .hivemind/state/session-context-prompt.md)
111: EXPECTED=$((OLD_COUNT + 1))
112: if [ "$NEW_COUNT" -ne "$EXPECTED" ]; then echo "FAIL: sessions_count mismatch"; fi
113: 
114: # Check last_updated is today
115: TODAY=$(date -u +%Y-%m-%d)
116: grep -q "last_updated:.*$TODAY" .hivemind/state/session-context-prompt.md || echo "FAIL: last_updated not today"
117: ```
118: 
119: ## Complexity Assessment
120: 
121: New content complexity is assessed on a 1-10 scale:
122: 
123: | Score | Criteria |
124: |-------|----------|
125: | 1-2 | Single source, no cross-references, linear narrative |
126: | 3-4 | Multiple sources, same domain, minor cross-references |
127: | 5-6 | Multiple domains, conflicting information, actor relationships |
128: | 7-8 | Cross-domain dependencies, temporal complexity, unresolved conflicts |
129: | 9-10 | Multi-system integration, high uncertainty, critical decision points |
130: 
131: The stored `complexity` is `max(existing_complexity, new_assessment)` capped at 10.
132: 
133: ## Initialization (First Absorb)
134: 
135: When the target file exists but lacks absorb-specific fields, initialize them:
136: 
137: ```yaml
138: # Add these fields to existing YAML frontmatter
139: dates_active: [2026-04-09]
140: actors: []
141: domains: []
142: sessions_count: 1
143: complexity: <assessed>
144: absorb_history:
145:   - date: 2026-04-09
146:     wave_count: 4
147:     sources_added: <count>
148:     sections_added: <count>
149: version: 1
150: ```
151: 
152: Preserve ALL existing YAML fields. Only ADD new fields, never remove.
153: 
154: ## Edge Cases
155: 
156: ### Missing Fields
157: 
158: If `sessions_count` doesn't exist → assume 0, then increment to 1.
159: If `actors` doesn't exist → create empty list, then append.
160: If `absorb_history` doesn't exist → create list with first entry.
161: If `version` doesn't exist → set to 1.
162: 
163: ### Corrupt YAML
164: 
165: If YAML parse fails:
166: 1. Extract body content (everything after second `---`)
167: 2. Reconstruct YAML from scratch using known fields
168: 3. Log the reconstruction in absorb_history: `{note: "yaml_reconstructed"}`
169: 4. Continue with Wave 4
170: 
171: ### Concurrent Modification
172: 
173: If the file was modified between Wave 0 read and Wave 4 write:
174: 1. Re-read the file
175: 2. Re-apply merge operations against the new content
176: 3. Append the absorb-session block
177: 4. Retry up to 3 times
178: 5. If still failing → escalate to user
179: 
180: ## Complete Example
181: 
182: ### Before (existing file):
183: ```yaml
184: ---
185: phase: execution
186: phase_index: 2
187: sessions_count: 2
188: complexity: 5
189: dates_active: [2026-04-07, 2026-04-08]
190: actors:
191:   - name: "Auth Service"
192:     first_seen: "2026-04-07"
193: domains: [authentication, api]
194: absorb_history:
195:   - date: 2026-04-08
196:     wave_count: 4
197:     sources_added: 3
198:     sections_added: 2
199: version: 2
200: last_updated: "2026-04-08T16:00:00Z"
201: ---
202: 
203: # Existing Session Notes
204: Previous absorb covered auth module analysis.
205: ```
206: 
207: ### After (new absorb with 2 new URLs, 1 new actor, 1 new domain):
208: ```yaml

210: phase: execution
211: phase_index: 2
212: sessions_count: 3
213: complexity: 7
214: dates_active: [2026-04-07, 2026-04-08, 2026-04-09]

218:   - name: "Payment Gateway"
219:     first_seen: "2026-04-09"

226:   - date: 2026-04-09
227:     wave_count: 4
228:     sources_added: 2

241:   </sources>

244:     The Auth Service tokens are used for payment authorization headers.
245:   </narrative>

257:   </insights>

261: ```
262:

}
```

**Output:**
```
<path>/Users/apple/hivemind-plugin/.worktrees/harness-experiment/.opencode/skills/hf-context-absorb/references/03-xml-body-schema.md</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>
1: # XML Body Schema
2: 
3: ## Overview
4: 
5: Absorbed content is appended to the body of `session-context-prompt.md` using structured XML blocks. Each absorb session produces one `<absorb-session>` element containing structured sub-elements.
6: 
7: ## Root Element
8: 
9: ```xml
10: <absorb-session date="YYYY-MM-DD" wave_count="4">
11:   <!-- Child elements -->
12: </absorb-session>
13: ```
14: 
15: ### Attributes
16: 
17: | Attribute | Type | Required | Description |
18: |-----------|------|----------|-------------|
19: | `date` | ISO date | Yes | Date of the absorb session (YYYY-MM-DD) |
20: | `wave_count` | integer | Yes | Number of waves completed (typically 4) |
21: 
22: ## Child Elements
23: 
24: ### `<sources>`
25: 
26: Container for all input sources processed during this absorb.
27: 
28: ```xml
29: <sources>
30:   <source type="url" path="https://example.com/doc" extracted="true" />
31:   <source type="url" path="https://example.com/behind-paywall" extracted="false" failure_reason="403 Forbidden" />
32:   <source type="file" path="src/auth/login.ts" extracted="true" />
33:   <source type="file" path="docs/architecture.md" extracted="true" depth="SCAN" />
34:   <source type="text" path="inline:user-message-paragraph-3" extracted="true" />
35: </sources>
36: ```
37: 
38: #### `<source>` Attributes
39: 
40: | Attribute | Type | Required | Values | Description |
41: |-----------|------|----------|--------|-------------|
42: | `type` | enum | Yes | `url`, `file`, `text` | Source type classification |
43: | `path` | string | Yes | URL, file path, or inline reference | Source identifier |
44: | `extracted` | boolean | Yes | `true`, `false` | Whether content was successfully extracted |
45: | `failure_reason` | string | Only if extracted=false | Any string | Why extraction failed |
46: | `depth` | enum | Only for type=file | `SKIM`, `SCAN`, `DEEP` | Reading depth used |
47: 
48: ### `<narrative>`
49: 
50: Synthesized narrative from Wave 2B. Contains prose text organized into paragraphs.
51: 
52: ```xml
53: <narrative>
54:   <main_story>Payment integration follows Stripe's recommended server-side flow.</main_story>
55: 
56:   <subplot name="webhook-integration">
57:     Webhook endpoints must verify Stripe signatures before processing events.
58:     The verification uses the STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET environment variable.
59:   </subplot>
60: 
61:   <subplot name="auth-reuse">
62:     Existing JWT tokens from the Auth Service are reused for payment API authorization.
63:     No separate payment auth is needed.
64:   </subplot>
65: </narrative>
66: ```
67: 
68: #### `<narrative>` Sub-elements
69: 
70: | Element | Required | Description |
71: |---------|----------|-------------|
72: | `<main_story>` | Yes | 1-3 sentence summary of the main narrative |
73: | `<subplot>` | No, repeatable | Named sub-plots with prose content. Has `name` attribute. |
74: 
75: ### `<entities>`
76: 
77: Structured list of actors and domains discovered during this absorb.
78: 
79: ```xml
80: <entities>
81:   <actor name="Payment Gateway" first_seen="2026-04-09" type="external-service" />
82:   <actor name="Auth Service" first_seen="2026-04-07" type="internal-module" />
83:   <actor name="John Developer" first_seen="2026-04-09" type="person" />
84:   <domain name="payments" />
85:   <domain name="webhooks" />
86:   <domain name="authentication" status="previously-known" />
87: </entities>
88: ```
89: 
90: #### `<actor>` Attributes
91: 
92: | Attribute | Type | Required | Description |
93: |-----------|------|----------|-------------|
94: | `name` | string | Yes | Unique actor identifier |
95: | `first_seen` | date | Yes | ISO date when actor first appeared |
96: | `type` | enum | No | `person`, `team`, `internal-module`, `external-service`, `system`, `concept` |
97: 
98: #### `<domain>` Attributes
99: 
100: | Attribute | Type | Required | Description |
101: |-----------|------|----------|-------------|
102: | `name` | string | Yes | Domain/topic name |
103: | `status` | enum | No | `new`, `previously-known` (defaults to `new`) |
104: 
105: ### `<timeline>`
106: 
107: Chronologically ordered events extracted from the input.
108: 
109: ```xml
110: <timeline>
111:   <event date="2026-04-07" description="Auth module audit began" confidence="confirmed" />
112:   <event date="2026-04-08" description="JWT token flow documented" confidence="confirmed" />
113:   <event date="2026-04-09" description="Payment integration requirements gathered" confidence="confirmed" />
114:   <event date="2026-04-10" description="Webhook implementation expected" confidence="inferred" />
115: </timeline>
116: ```
117: 
118: #### `<event>` Attributes
119: 
120: | Attribute | Type | Required | Description |
121: |-----------|------|----------|-------------|
122: | `date` | date or date-range | Yes | When the event occurred or will occur |
123: | `description` | string | Yes | What happened |
124: | `confidence` | enum | Yes | `confirmed` (sourced), `inferred` (from context), `speculative` (best guess) |
125: 
126: ### `<insights>`
127: 
128: Key findings, cross-references, and synthesis results.
129: 
130: ```xml
131: <insights>
132:   <finding source="cross-ref" confidence="high">
133:     Payment auth reuses existing JWT tokens from Auth Service.
134:     Evidence: stripe-node docs show Bearer token pattern; login.ts exports token generator.
135:   </finding>
136: 
137:   <finding source="url-extraction" confidence="high">
138:     Webhook signature verification is critical for payment confirmation.
139:     Evidence: Stripe docs require signature verification on all webhook endpoints.
140:   </finding>
141: 
142:   <finding source="narrative-synthesis" confidence="medium">
143:     The payment flow appears to be in early planning stage based on the questions asked.
144:     Evidence: No implementation code found, only requirements documents.
145:   </finding>
146: </insights>
147: ```
148: 
149: #### `<finding>` Attributes
150: 
151: | Attribute | Type | Required | Description |
152: |-----------|------|----------|-------------|
153: | `source` | enum | Yes | `url-extraction`, `file-scan`, `cross-ref`, `narrative-synthesis`, `clarification` |
154: | `confidence` | enum | Yes | `high`, `medium`, `low` |
155: 
156: ### `<questions_open>`
157: 
158: Unresolved ambiguities from Wave 3. May be empty.
159: 
160: ```xml
161: <questions_open>
162:   <question id="q1" source="https://docs.stripe.com/webhooks" asked_user="false">
163:     Does the webhook endpoint need idempotency handling?
164:     Stripe docs mention it but the requirements don't specify.
165:   </question>
166: 
167:   <question id="q2" source="src/auth/login.ts" asked_user="true" answer="deferred">
168:     Should payment tokens have a shorter TTL than auth tokens?
169:     User deferred this decision.
170:   </question>
171: </questions_open>
172: ```
173: 
174: #### `<question>` Attributes
175: 
176: | Attribute | Type | Required | Description |
177: |-----------|------|----------|-------------|
178: | `id` | string | Yes | Unique question identifier within this absorb (q1, q2, ...) |
179: | `source` | string | Yes | URL or file path where ambiguity was found |
180: | `asked_user` | boolean | Yes | Whether this was asked in Wave 3 |
181: | `answer` | enum | No | `resolved`, `deferred`, `unanswerable` |
182: 
183: ## Nesting Rules
184: 
185: 1. `<absorb-session>` is always a top-level element in the body
186: 2. Child elements MUST appear in this order: `sources`, `narrative`, `entities`, `timeline`, `insights`, `questions_open`
187: 3. All child elements are optional EXCEPT `sources` and `narrative`
188: 4. Multiple `<absorb-session>` blocks are separated by blank lines
189: 5. No nested `<absorb-session>` elements
190: 
191: ## Content Encoding Rules
192: 
193: 1. Escape XML special characters in text content: `&` → `&amp;`, `<` → `&lt;`, `>` → `&gt;`
194: 2. Do not use CDATA sections — use entity escaping instead
195: 3. Code snippets go inside `<finding>` or `<narrative>` prose, wrapped in backtick-style markers
196: 4. URLs in attribute values do NOT need escaping (they're quoted)
197: 5. Long prose in elements: use multiple lines, no wrapping within XML tags
198: 
199: ## Validation Checklist
200: 
201: After constructing the XML block:
202: 
203: ```
204: [ ] <absorb-session> has date and wave_count attributes
205: [ ] <sources> present with at least one <source>
206: [ ] Every <source> has type, path, and extracted attributes
207: [ ] <narrative> present with <main_story>
208: [ ] <entities> lists all actors mentioned in <narrative>
209: [ ] <timeline> events are in chronological order
210: [ ] <insights> findings cite their source
211: [ ] <questions_open> present (may be empty)
212: [ ] No unescaped XML special characters in text content
213: [ ] Child elements in correct order
214: ```

(End of file - total 214 lines)
</content>
```

### KEY ENTITY EXTRACTION SUMMARY

**Primary Actors/Modules:**
- `HarnessControlPlane` — plugin entry point (composition root)
- `HarnessLifecycleManager` — session lifecycle state machine
- `continuity.ts/continuity-clone.ts/continuity-normalizers.ts` — durable state persistence
- `background-manager.ts` — background agent execution
- `delegation-packet.ts` — task delegation construction
- `specialist-router.ts` — agent routing
- `governance-engine.ts` — governance persistence
- `injection-engine.ts` — context injection
- `concurrency.ts` — keyed semaphore
- `lifecycle-process-runner.ts` — process execution
- `lifecycle-background-observer.ts` — background session monitoring

**Domain Terms:**
- Runtime composition engine, CQRS, two-halves architecture, Hard Harness, Soft Meta-Concepts
- Granularity atoms, chain-breaking design, 2-end-extreme metrics
- Delegation chain, task persistence, session recovery, background agents
- Auto-loop/Ralph-loop, category system, specialist routing
- Product-detox (anti-pattern), skill proliferation, agent triplication
- GSD (Get Shit Done) workflow system
- HiveFiver meta-builder system
- Detox-refactor skill network

**Cross-File Relationships (key dependency chains):**
1. `plugin.ts` → `src/hooks/*` + `src/tools/*` + `src/lib/*` (composition root imports all)
2. `lifecycle-manager.ts` → `continuity.ts` → `state.ts` (state chain)
3. `continuity.ts` → `continuity-clone.ts` + `continuity-normalizers.ts` (persistence helpers)
4. `.opencode/plugins/harness-control-plane.ts` → `dist/plugin.js` → `src/plugin.ts` (loading chain)
5. `.planning/PROJECT.md` → `.planning/ROADMAP.md` → `.planning/phases/02-*` (planning chain)
6. `.opencode/agents/`, `.opencode/skills/`, `.opencode/commands/` → symlinked to `.hivefiver-meta-builder/` (shared config)

**Notable Gaps/Absences:**
- `src/cli/` — empty directory (CLI substrate not yet implemented)
- `src/harness/` — empty directory
- `src/kernel/` — empty directory
- `src/plugins/` — empty directory
- Phase 3-7 plans not yet created in `.planning/phases/`
- Only 5 runtime tests mentioned in diagnostic (but 533 total tests claimed)

## Assistant (Hivefiver-Orchestrator · GLM-5.1 · 285.6s)

**Tool: task**

**Input:**
```json
{
  "description": "Wave 2B: Narrative Synthesis",
  "prompt": "You are the subagent **Wave 2B: Narrative Synthesis** for the hf-context-absorb skill. You must do as this prompt instructs and know that you are being delegated. As subagent you cannot delegate further, and you must fulfill your work. 284: - All cross-references between skills resolve to existing artifacts
285: - Progressive disclosure enforced in all skill content
286: - No placeholder or "nothingness" content in any skill

290: 
291: Begins only after Tier 1 exits successfully.
292:

294:

296: quality criteria:
297: 
298: 1. **Description accuracy** — Does the agent's description match its actual role?
299: 2. **Tool assignments** — Are referenced tools available and correctly specified?
300: 3. **Permission model** — Are permissions minimal and justified?
301: 4. **Cross-references** — Does the agent reference existing skills/commands?
302: 5. **Temperature/model config** — Is configuration appropriate for the agent's task?
303: 6. **Trigger conditions** — When does this agent activate? Is it clear?
304:

373: 
374: <risks_mitigated>
375: 
376: ## Risk 1: Context Bomb (oh-my-openagent-full.xml)
377: - **Risk**: 11MB XML file (276K lines) will blow context window if read fully
378: - **Mitigation**: NEVER read the full file. Use `grep` with targeted patterns,
379:   or read SKILL.md (1.7KB) which summarizes the reference. If deep patterns are
380:   needed, use chunked offset reads of max 200 lines at a time.
381: - **Status**: Mitigated by constraint #8
382: 
383: ## Risk 2: 70 Uncommitted Files
384: - **Risk**: Working on top of uncommitted changes means no rollback point
385: - **Mitigation**: Commit a checkpoint before starting (pre-flight step)
386: - **Status**: Mitigated by pre-flight gate
387: 
388: ## Risk 3: Concurrent Writes
389: - **Risk**: Multiple agents modifying files simultaneously → merge conflicts
390: - **Mitigation**: Sequential execution enforced. One artifact at a time.
391: - **Status**: Mitigated by constraint #7
392: 
393: ## Risk 4: Broken eval-harness Symlink
394: - **Risk**: Symlink at `.opencode/skills/eval-harness` points to non-existent target
395: - **Mitigation**: Remove or fix the symlink in pre-flight before skills audit begins
396: - **Status**: Identified, fix required in pre-flight
397: 
398: ## Risk 5: Unbounded Loop Cycles
399: - **Risk**: A skill might never reach 100% on skill-judge, causing infinite loops
400: - **Mitigation**: Hard cap of 3 audit-refactor cycles per artifact. After 3 failures,
401:   escalate to user with documented exception.
402: - **Status**: Mitigated by per-skill cycle definition
403: 
404: ## Risk 6: Cross-Reference Drift
405: - **Risk**: Fixing one artifact breaks references in another
406: - **Mitigation**: Skills are audited first (foundation tier). Agent refs to skills
407:   are validated after skills are locked. Commands after agents. Workflows last.
408:   This ensures downstream references always point to already-validated upstream artifacts.
409: - **Status**: Mitigated by tier ordering
410: 
411: ## Risk 7: .opencode/ is Real Copies (not symlinks)
412: - **Risk**: Changes to .opencode/ won't propagate to labs automatically
413: - **Mitigation**: Document which is canonical source for each artifact. If labs are
414:   canonical, sync changes back after .opencode/ is updated.
415: - **Status**: Mitigated by constraint #9
416: 
417: ## Risk 8: Progressive Disclosure Not Enforced
418: - **Risk**: Skills may pass audit on content quality but fail on structure
419: - **Mitigation**: Progressive disclosure is a specific dimension in skill-judge
420:   (15 points). Skills cannot score 100% without proper layering.
421: - **Status**: Mitigated by skill-judge dimension 2
422: 
423: </risks_mitigated>

path=\"inline:hivemind-philosophy-5-pillars\" extracted=\"true\" />\n  </sources>\n\n  <narrative>\n    <main_story>\n      HiveMind V3 is a runtime composition engine for OpenCode that evolved from a bloated 15,000-LOC anti-pattern (product-detox) into a disciplined ~8,100-LOC clean harness implementing a two-halves architecture: a \"Hard Harness\" npm package (tools, hooks, plugin assembly) and \"Soft Meta-Concepts\" (skills, agents, commands in .opencode/). The project's philosophy — \"Agent Intelligence = HIVE + MIND\" — means agents gain intelligence through hierarchical collaboration within the HIVE while sharing one MIND with their human operator. It is currently at 17/18 verified truths on Phase 2, blocked by a single runtime-policy override persistence gap.\n    </main_story>\n\n    <subplot name=\"5-pillars-philosophy\">\n      The HiveMind philosophy rests on 5 pillars: (1) Hierarchical Superiority — systematic file trees with safe dependency ordering; (2) Collaborative Domains — agents bounded by domain, delegation controlled within boundaries, reports flowing up and down; (3) Strategically Measurable — 2-end-extreme metrics requiring both quantitative AND qualitative proof, incremental guardrails; (4) Iteratively Granular — break down small (max 300 LOC per file), loop until perfect; (5) Growing MEMS-BRAIN — long-term intelligence collected by HIVE, shared toward MIND (content TBD — user wants crawled from worktrees).\n    </subplot>\n\n    <subplot name=\"framework-differentiation\">\n      HiveMind explicitly differentiates from GSD/BMAD (corporate-spec-driven frameworks requiring procedural compliance) and OMO/Oh-my-opencode (all-in-SOTA-harness for full autonomous coding). Position: \"ready to be either if users configure it\" — a runtime composition engine that can adopt other frameworks' patterns through its Tier 3 skills layer without committing to any single paradigm.\n    </subplot>\n\n    <subplot name=\"detox-arc\">\n      The product-detox branch poisoned the codebase with 235 SKILL.md files (target: ~20), 22 governance scripts that dictated instead of reporting, 57 agent file copies, and a 1,121-line god-tool. The architecture proposal (2026-04-04) defined this as the anti-pattern and established the clean two-halves target of ~2,547 LOC. Seven worktrees now contain different evolution stages.\n    </subplot>\n\n    <subplot name=\"7-phase-roadmap\">\n      Phase 1 (Baseline Cleanup) achieved 7/10 items. Phase 2 (V3 Runtime Architecture) completed all 9 plans across 9 waves but 1 of 18 verification truths remains open (runtimePolicyOverride gap). Phases 3-7 (Schema Definition through Runtime Domain Restructuring) are planned but gated on Phase 2 reaching 18/18.\n    </subplot>\n\n    <subplot name=\"cqrs-enforcement\">\n      Tools are write-side (5 core tools with Zod schemas that mutate state), hooks are read-side (event observers that inject context, never mutate), and the plugin assembly is 57 LOC with zero business logic. Dependency rules enforce types.ts as leaf, max module 500 LOC, no circular dependencies.\n    </subplot>\n\n    <subplot name=\"skill-assessment-next-cycles\">\n      User identified skill gaps: TDD, spec-driven, planning skills still lacking. ## Assistant (Compaction · GLM-5.1 · 73.7s)

_Thinking:_

The user wants a detailed summary of our conversation for continuing the work.

## Goal

The user is building the **HiveMind** project — a runtime composition engine for OpenCode that provides multi-agent orchestration, context governance, and a meta-builder system. The immediate task was to absorb a massive amount of context (worktree file listings, Hivemind philosophy documents, 5 Pillars framework, skill assessment instructions) into the project's persistent session state using the `hf-context-absorb` skill's multi-wave protocol.

The broader goal spans three large document artifacts:
1. **Document 1 (briefed this session)**: Concepts, visions, and philosophies — the "HIVE + MIND" philosophy and 5 Pillars
2. **Document 2 (not yet started)**: Architecture and infrastructure — "THE WAYS" of how a harness should work
3. **Document 3 (not yet started)**: Agents team and context pipelines harness toward the architecture

## Instructions

- **Always use the `hf-context-absorb` skill** when absorbing context — it defines a 5-wave protocol (Wave 0: State Load, Wave 1: Outline Formation, Wave 2: Deep Processing, Wave 3: Clarification, Wave 4: Assemble & Append)
- **NEVER overwrite** `.hivemind/state/session-context-prompt.md` — always APPEND
- **YAML merge rules**: `sessions_count` INCREMENT, `last_updated` OVERWRITE, `actors` MERGE-APPEND, `domains` APPEND if new, `absorb_history` APPEND entry, `complexity` RECOMPUTE as max(existing, new). PRESERVE all unknown fields.
- **XML body schema**: New content appended as `<absorb-session>` blocks with child elements in order: `sources`, `narrative`, `entities`, `timeline`, `insights`, `questions_open`
- **Delegation**: Delegate waves to subagents via task tool. Background delegation is unstable — delegate to orchestra agent so it runs downstream while horizontal work continues
- **Session exports**: Files matching `*ses*` or `*session*` are full session records — very lengthy, only SKIM
- **Skills mentioned for next cycles**: skill-creator, skill-development, skill-review, skill-judge — these help assess bundles for conflicts, overlaps, gaps
- **5 Pillars practice**: (1) Hierarchical Superiority — systematic file trees, safe dependency ordering; (2) Collaborative Domains — delegation within domains, reports up/down; (3) Strategically Measurable — end-to-end quantitative+qualitative metrics; (4) Iteratively Granular — break small, loop until perfect; (5) Growing MEMS-BRAIN — long-term intelligence (TBD, user wants crawled from worktrees)

## Discoveries

- **Architecture tier conflict**: `architecture-proposal-hivemind-v3.md` defines 2 halves (Hard Harness + Soft Meta-Concepts) while `hivemind-current-state.md` defines 3 Tiers. Resolution: different documents for different purposes — both valid in context.
- **LOC budget exceeded**: AGENTS.md targets ~4,000-5,000 LOC but `src/` is ~8,100 LOC across 52 TypeScript files (6,339 in `src/lib/` alone).
- **3 orphan modules**: `governance-engine.ts`, `specialist-router.ts`, `injection-engine.ts` exist on disk but are absent from architecture proposal and session state.
- **CQRS pattern**: Tools are write-side (Zod schemas, mutate state), hooks are read-side (event observers, inject context). `plugin.ts` is only 57 LOC — meets the <100 LOC target.
- **7 worktrees exist**: harness-experiment (primary), hivefiver-agent-cmd-packs, hivefiver-packs, hivefiver-v2 (duplicate of packs), product-detox (anti-pattern reference), session-journal-minimal (built version). Merge strategy unclear.
- **Pillar 5 (MEMS-BRAIN)**: User hasn't defined it yet — asked agents to "crawl from worktrees intensively" to synthesize the concept.
- **Skill gaps identified by user**: TDD, spec-driven, planning skills are lacking. Next cycles need: assess bundles for conflicts/overlaps, map skill-agent-workflow pairings, form red fail cases.
- **Existing session state was 596 lines** covering a prior absorb about delegation failure forensics and bundle scan failures.

## WE ARE NOT:

- The corporate-spec-driven-frame-work-maniac for the nerds: unlike GSD, BMAD or any framework that at the top 5 most-used requiring users must be adept and constraint into the particular technology and vibe-coding dev trend requiring certain procedures, segregating very clear between “autonomous” = “following strict rules and protocols” → BUT WE ARE READY TO BE SO, as long as the users set us up to.

<skill_content name="hm-detective">
# Skill: hm-detective

# HM Detective

The strategic investigation and retrieval skill. Teaches agents HOW to read, navigate, search, and edit efficiently — not what to research, but how to consume information without blowing context budgets.

## Quick Jump

| Investigation Need | Section | Jump |
|--------------------|---------|------|
| "How do I read this?" | Reading Modes | [Three Reading Modes](#three-reading-modes) |
| "How much context will this cost?" | Token Budget | [references/token-budget.md](references/token-budget.md) |
| "I lost context — recover" | Swarm Recovery | [references/swarm-recovery.md](references/swarm-recovery.md) |
| "What tech stack is this?" | Tech Registry | [references/tech-registry.md](references/tech-registry.md) |
| "How do I edit safely?" | Surgical Edits | [references/surgical-edits.md](references/surgical-edits.md) |
| "Where do notes go?" | Document Pipeline | [references/document-pipeline.md](references/document-pipeline.md) |

## Three Reading Modes

Every file read costs tokens. Choose the cheapest mode that answers your question.

| Mode | Token Cost | When | Tools |
|------|-----------|------|-------|
| **SKIM** | ~5% | Orientation: "what is this?" | glob, ls, frontmatter-only, grep -c |
| **SCAN** | ~15% | Targeted: "find X" | grep -n, offset reads ±20 lines, TOC navigation |
| **DEEP** | 100% | Understanding: "need every line" | Read full file, repomix pack + grep |

**Escalation rule**: START → SKIM → (if insufficient) SCAN → (if still need context) DEEP. Never skip to DEEP.

### Mode Selection Decision Tree

```
What do you need?
|
+-- "What files exist?" or "What is this project?"
|   -> SKIM: glob patterns, ls directory, grep -c for match counts
|
+-- "Where is function X defined?" or "What imports Y?"
|   -> SCAN: grep -n "pattern" file → get line numbers → offset read ±20
|
+-- "How does this algorithm work?" or "I need to understand every branch"
|   -> DEEP: Read full file (only after SKIM + SCAN confirm it's the right file)
```

### Case Study: Finding a Bug in a 600-Line File

**Wrong**: Read the entire 600-line file. Cost: ~600 lines of context.

**Right**:
1. SKIM: `grep -c "error" file.ts` → 12 matches. File is relevant.
2. SCAN: `grep -n "error" file.ts` → lines 45, 120, 234, 310, 445, 501, 520, 533, 540, 555, 567, 580
3. SCAN: Read offset=40 limit=30 (lines 40-70), offset=115 limit=30 (lines 115-145), etc.
4. DEEP: Only if the bug spans multiple sections you've already identified.

**Cost**: ~200 lines vs 600 lines. 67% savings.

## Token-Efficient Retrieval Patterns

These patterns apply across all reading modes. Master them before any investigation.

| Pattern | How | Savings |
|---------|-----|---------|
| **Offset Hop-Reading** | Read offset=N limit=30 instead of reading N lines to get to line N | 90%+ vs full read |
| **Grep-Before-Read** | grep -n → get line numbers → offset read only those sections | 80%+ vs blind read |
| **Frontmatter-Only** | For planning docs, read only between --- markers | 95%+ vs full doc |
| **TOC-First** | grep ## headings first, then targeted reads | 70%+ vs full read |
| **Repomix Compress** | Always use compress: true (70% token reduction) | 70% vs uncompressed |

### Worked Example: Finding Where a Function Is Called

**Goal**: Find all callers of `processTask` in a 47-file codebase.

```
Step 1 (SKIM): grep -rn "processTask" src/ --include="*.ts" | wc -l → 23 matches
Step 2 (SKIM): grep -rn "processTask" src/ --include="*.ts" | cut -d: -f1 | sort -u → 8 files
Step 3 (SCAN): For each of 8 files, grep -n "processTask" → get line numbers
Step 4 (SCAN): Read ±20 lines around each call site (8 files × ~2 calls × 40 lines = 640 lines)
Step 5 (DEEP): Only if a call site's context is unclear after SCAN
```

**Cost**: ~700 lines total vs reading all 47 files (~14,000 lines). **95% savings**.

---

## Hierarchical Tech Registry

The `.tech-registry.json` file is your persistent memory across sessions. Read it FIRST before any investigation.

### What It Contains

- **Stack**: Language, runtime, framework, test tool, build tool
- **Modules**: Every source file with its role (leaf/core/entry), LOC, and dependencies
- **Concerns**: Active issues and resolved problems

### Read-First Protocol

```
1. Read .tech-registry.json
2. If exists → use stack for conventions, modules for dependency graph
3. If missing → run discovery (see references/tech-registry.md)
4. If stale → spot-check 3 files, update if mismatched
```

### Update Protocol

Agents APPEND findings — never overwrite. After discovering new information:
1. Read the full registry
2. Modify the specific field that changed
3. Update `last_updated` to today's date
4. Write the complete file back

See [references/tech-registry.md](references/tech-registry.md) for full schema and procedures.

---

## Swarm-Based Context Recovery

When context is lost (compaction, interruption, session reset), dispatch 5 parallel agents. Each returns max 100 lines.

| Agent | Task | Output |
|-------|------|--------|
| **TOC Agent** | Read heading structures → section map with line ranges | File → Section → Line Range → Purpose |
| **Metadata Agent** | Read all frontmatter → status, key_files, commits | File → name → status → key_files |
| **Git Agent** | git log --oneline -20, git diff --stat HEAD~5 | Timeline + changed files |
| **Diff Agent** | Read diffs for changed files only → what changed | File → Lines +/- → Summary |
| **Registry Agent** | Read .tech-registry.json → known tech stack | Full registry or inferred stack |

### Merge Procedure

1. Collect all 5 agent outputs
2. Create `.scratch/recovery-brief-YYYY-MM-DD.md`
3. Structure: Project State → Recent Changes → Document Map → What Was In Progress → Gaps → Next Actions
4. Validate: all 5 agents returned, brief < 500 lines, gaps documented
5. Update tech registry with any new discoveries

See [references/swarm-recovery.md](references/swarm-recovery.md) for full prompt envelopes and merge procedures.

---

## LSP-Aware Surgical Edit Protocol

Every edit follows this 5-step sequence. No shortcuts.

1. **Locate**: `grep -n "target" file` → exact line numbers
2. **Read Context**: Read offset=(line-20) limit=40 → context ±20
3. **Edit**: Use PRECISE oldString (exact whitespace, indentation, newlines)
4. **Verify Size**: NEVER edit >50 lines in one operation
5. **Verify Result**: `grep` the result to confirm it landed correctly

### LSP Safety Rules

- Changing exported function signatures? Update all callers first, or use overloads
- Adding new symbols? Use unique names to avoid collisions
- Renaming variables? Sequential edits, one per usage, verify each

See [references/surgical-edits.md](references/surgical-edits.md) for before/after examples and anti-patterns.

---

## Document Promotion Pipeline

Investigation artifacts flow through four stages with increasing quality requirements:

```
.scratch/              → Raw notes (ephemeral, session-scoped)
  ↓ promote (sources cited, no TODOs)
.research/             → Findings with sources (reusable across sessions)
  ↓ promote (decision stated, alternatives considered)
.planning/decisions/   → ADRs (Architecture Decision Records, project-level)
  ↓ promote (success criteria, specific files, verification commands)
.planning/phases/      → Execution plans (Source of Truth for implementation)
```

### Promotion Gates

| Gate | Requirement |
|------|-------------|
| Scratch → Research | Every finding has a source, no TODOs, organized by topic |
| Research → Decision | Decision in one sentence, 2+ alternatives considered, consequences listed |
| Decision → Plan | References ADRs, checkable success criteria, specific files, verification commands |

See [references/document-pipeline.md](references/document-pipeline.md) for naming conventions and content structures.

## Anti-Patterns — STOP When You Detect These

| Anti-Pattern | Detection | Fix |
|-------------|-----------|-----|
| Full File Fever | Reading >200 lines when you need 3 | grep → offset read |
| Context Avalanche | Loading 5+ files "for context" | Skim first, deep-read only targets |
| Registry Amnesia | Re-discovering tech stack each session | Read .tech-registry.json FIRST |
| Edit Blast Zone | Editing >50 lines in one operation | Surgical edits: grep → offset ±20 → precise oldString |
| Solo Recovery | One agent reading massive session export | 5-agent swarm |

## References (Progressive Disclosure)

Load references ONLY when the SKILL.md procedures are insufficient for your task.

- **[Reading Modes](references/reading-modes.md)** — Detailed procedures with worked examples for SKIM, SCAN, DEEP
- **[Token Budget](references/token-budget.md)** — Cost tables, estimation formulas, escalation rules
- **[Swarm Recovery](references/swarm-recovery.md)** — 5-agent protocol, prompt envelopes, merge procedures
- **[Tech Registry](references/tech-registry.md)** — Schema, update procedures, cross-session persistence
- **[Surgical Edits](references/surgical-edits.md)** — LSP-aware edit protocol with before/after examples
- **[Document Pipeline](references/document-pipeline.md)** — Promotion rules, validation gates, naming conventions

## When NOT to Load References

| Condition | Do NOT Load | Reason |
|-----------|-------------|--------|
| Simple file lookup (< 3 files) | All references | SKILL.md has enough for basic navigation |
| Only need token estimates | reading-modes.md, swarm-recovery.md | Load only token-budget.md |
| Already know the tech stack | tech-registry.md | Read .tech-registry.json directly |
| Context > 50% consumed | ALL references | Use cheapest mode available, document gaps |
| Single-file edit | surgical-edits.md | Follow the 5-step protocol from SKILL.md |
